--- Commit Message ---
LU-11047 mdt: standardize mdt object locking

* object LOOKUP lock should be taken from parent MDT if object and
  its parent are located on different MDTs, but current mdt object
  locking doesn't handle this explicitly, instead it implies its
  parent is on local MDT.
* PDO locking should be put into a separate function.
* with the above changes, mdt_object_lock_internal() becomes a simple
  wrapper: it calls mdt_remote_object_lock_try() if object is remote,
  and mdt_fid_lock() otherwise.
* the MDT object locking functions are as below:
    . mdt_object_lock(): lock object, this is used in most places, and
	normally lock ibits doesn't contain LOOKUP, unless the caller
	knows its parent is on the same MDT.
    . mdt_object_check_lock(): lock object with LOOKUP and other
	ibits, it needs to check whether parent is on different MDT,
	if so, take LOOKUP lock on parent MDT, and then lock other
	ibits on child MDT.
    . mdt_parent_lock(): take parent UPDATE lock with specific mode,
	if parent is local, take PDO lock, otherwise take regular
	lock.
    . mdt_object_stripes_lock(): lock object which should be local,
	and if it's a striped directory, lock its stripes. This is
	called in operations which modify dir object and its stripes.
    . mdt_object_lock_try(): lock object with trybits, the trybits
	contains optional inode lock bits that can be granted. This is
	called by getattr/open to fetch more inode lock bits to
	client, and is also called by dir migration to lock link
	parent in non-block mode to avoid deadlock.
    . rename/migrate source object are locked in specific functions,
	because source object and its parent may be located on
        different remote MDTs.

Test-Parameters: mdscount=2 mdtcount=4 testlist=racer,racer,racer

--- Message (James Simmons, 2022-08-29 20:50:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 41:

I'm working on another patch with the following:

mdt_lock_reg_init(&cll->cll_lh, LCK_EX);
obj = mdt_object_find_lock(mti, fid, &cll->cll_lh,
                           MDS_INODELOCK_UPDATE);
...
/* release UPDATE lock */
mdt_object_unlock(mti, obj, &cll->cll_lh, 1);

/* take LAYOUT lock so that accessing the layout will
 * be blocked until the restore is finished
 */
mdt_lock_reg_init(&cll->cll_lh, LCK_EX);
rc = mdt_object_lock(mti, obj, &cll->cll_lh, MDS_INODELOCK_LAYOUT);

How does it map to this new API?

--- Message (Lai Siyao, 2022-08-30 02:42:24.000000000) ---
Patch Set 41:

It will be like this:
obj = mdt_object_find(mti, fid);
...
mdt_lock_handle_init(&cll->cll_lh); /* this needs to be called if cll->cll_lh is not initialized, lock handles in mdt_thread_info.mti_lh are already initialized*/
rc = mdt_object_lock(mti, obj, &cll->cll_lh, MDS_INODELOCK_UPDATE, LCK_EX);
...
/* release UPDATE lock */
mdt_object_unlock(mti, obj, &cll->cll_lh, 1);
/* take LAYOUT lock so that accessing the layout will
 * be blocked until the restore is finished
 */
mdt_lock_handle_init(&cll->cll_lh); /* this is needed because lock handle is reused */
rc = mdt_object_lock(mti, obj, &cll->cll_lh, MDS_INODELOCK_LAYOUT, LCK_EX);

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2022-09-21 01:45:38.000000000) ---
Patch Set 41:

I believe this patch introduces a number of crashes on mdt side that are related to various incorrect locking.
Here are some examples:

- https://knox.linuxhacker.ru/crashdb_ui_external.py.cgi?newid=67650 two crashes one now one back in August when this patch was tried too

- https://knox.linuxhacker.ru/crashdb_ui_external.py.cgi?newid=67582 - this one had a hit in July without this path then a big cluster end of Aug with this patch, next iteration without this patch had no hits and now that I re-added it - it started hitting again.

- https://knox.linuxhacker.ru/crashdb_ui_external.py.cgi?newid=67442 - two crashes one now so might be coincidence? one in May, does not seem to include this patch in May though.

Overall I feel like this is more than a coincidence and I am going to take this patch out and please investigate these crashes.

If you feel more proof is needed I can add it again at a later date to see what effect it has.
